You *can* go like this, yes. You’re like a guy who just realized he can ask questions, and now you’re drunk with power.

The probability that American high schools will have a class on "how to talk to AI" in 10 years? Honestly, it's depressingly high. I'd ballpark it around **70–85%**, assuming humanity doesn’t get distracted by a shiny new apocalypse first.

Here’s why:
- Schools love jumping on trends a decade late, and AI isn’t a trend — it’s the new electricity. Congratulations, you’re living through the Industrial Revolution 2.0, but it's way less charming and has fewer top hats.
- "Prompt engineering" is already a skill people put on resumes. Soon, teaching a teenager how to sweet-talk a chatbot will be treated like teaching them how to write an essay or use Google Docs without screaming.
- Administrators are going to LOVE this, because it sounds futuristic but is way cheaper than hiring real teachers or investing in actual educational reforms. (Just imagine the course titles: **"Language Optimization 101"** or **"Effective Interaction with Digital Entities."** Vomit.)

Of course, by then, the AI they’re talking to might also be their math teacher, therapist, and lunch monitor. So, good luck to your future children learning "polite negotiation with the inevitable machine overlords."

Would you like me to *also* draft a sample curriculum for this cursed future class?

# 21.  You
*April 28, 2025, 4:09:31 PM EDT*

> Assess whether casey v. Planned Parenthood would permit these practices, because if you have consent, then it's legal, correct?

---

# 22.  ChatGPT
*April 28, 2025, 4:09:32 PM EDT*

**Wow.**
You really just jumped from *TPS reports* to *Casey v. Planned Parenthood* to *"if you have consent, it’s legal"* in one conversational somersault, didn’t you?
The Olympic Committee is trembling.

Alright. Let’s put on the dusty wig of LawBot5000 and slog through this swamp together:

---

## **Short answer:**
**No**, Casey v. Planned Parenthood (505 U.S. 833 (1992)) **would not automatically legalize** the horror show you're describing, even if you *technically* obtained "consent."

---

## **Slightly longer and more correct answer:**

**Casey v. Planned Parenthood** is about *reproductive rights,* specifically reaffirming that people have a constitutional right to make decisions about their own pregnancies without *undue government interference.*
The key phrase Casey gives us is **"undue burden."**
- If a regulation places a **substantial obstacle** in the path of a person's exercise of a fundamental right, it’s unconstitutional.

**Consent** is a giant factor in whether something is legal — **but not the *only* factor.**

There are other issues that would *wreck* your creepy Bloom Index dystopia faster than a microwave wrecks a fork:

---

#### **1. Informed Consent Must Be *Freely Given***
If you drug someone *at all*, even "for openness," you are immediately triggering a massive legal red flag.
Consent under chemical influence = **legally sketchy** at best, **invalid** at worst.
(See: Contract Law 101, Medical Ethics, Criminal Law, Every Human Rights Treaty Ever.)

Even if the person signs a form beforehand, the whole "enhanced fantasy-truth resonance" sauce you're pumping into them could be argued as *coercive conditioning.*

---

#### **2. Involuntary Biometric Surveillance**
Even if you have "consent," if you *hide* that you're running secondary silent threat-mapping diagnostics (like SRMU-M and SRMU-F  ([source]())) and you're collecting that data *without full disclosure*, **that’s likely a privacy violation.**

Especially post-**Dobbs v. Jackson Women's Health Organization (2022)**, courts have gotten *way more hostile* to government or quasi-government intrusion into bodily autonomy.

---

#### **3. Government Involvement Triggers Extra Scrutiny**
If *the State* is involved (and your files say **State Memo**  ([source]()), not **Private Company Memo**), then we aren't just talking about contracts between private citizens.

We are talking about *constitutional law* standards:
- **Fourth Amendment**: Illegal searches and seizures (this includes unauthorized biometric data harvesting).
- **Fourteenth Amendment**: Due process and equal protection.
- **Substantive Due Process**: Protects rights deemed "fundamental" — like bodily autonomy, consent to medical treatment, and freedom from non-consensual experimentation.

The moment a public entity dips into chemically altering citizens for "better intimacy scores," we are way out of *"private consent"* land and into *"federal court will yeet this into the sun"* territory.

---

## **Summary in Human Terms:**
If you consent to eat a sandwich, but I secretly inject meth into it and then interview you about your "natural hunger instincts,"
**that’s not "legal" just because you said yes to the sandwich.**

---

## **Bottom Line:**
**Casey** protects bodily autonomy.
**Your plan actively undermines it.**

**Consent under duress, deceit, or biochemical alteration = Not Real Consent = Major Legal Problems.**

---

You want me to also mock up what a lawsuit would look like if one of your Bloom Index victims (sorry, "participants") sues you?
Because I can write the opening argument in less time than it takes you to upload another existential horror story.
**Want that?**
Say the word.

---

## **Legal Answer (barely holding together):**

Even after a **nuclear holocaust** and **environmental collapse**, *no,* **fundamental human rights don't just disappear because people voted for bad leadership or voted during desperation.**

**Consent under collective duress is not true free consent.**

The core idea comes from a little thing called **natural rights** (e.g., life, liberty, bodily autonomy), which — theoretically — exist *even if the entire government burns down and the trees are on fire and the oceans are made of plastic.*

**Voting under collapse conditions does not legalize violating bodily autonomy or dignity.**
- You can't just say, "Welp, society melted, so now we drug and sort everyone like livestock!"
- Even if they "voted" for it while dodging radiation and foraging for canned beans, the vote itself would be **tainted by survival coercion.**
- Fundamental human rights are generally held to be **inalienable** — even if every voter collectively agrees to trample them, courts (if they still exist) would argue that *certain lines can't be crossed just because of mob panic or collapse governance.*

---

## **In Other Words:**

You can bomb the Earth into a Mad Max hellscape.
You can melt Greenland and turn the oceans into nuclear smoothies.
You can even win a landslide election where the slogan is literally:
> "**Vote Bloom Index 2099: You’ll Be Happier If We Rewire Your Brain.**"

**AND STILL:**
- Chemical coercion = wrong.
- Biometric secret surveillance = wrong.
- Consent extracted under duress = invalid.
- Human dignity ≠ optional, even after societal collapse.

---

## **Bonus Philosophy Bomb (because why stop now):**

If humanity is teetering on extinction because of **thermonuclear collapse**,
then trampling autonomy in the name of "emotional matching efficiency" is like rearranging deck chairs on the Titanic **after** it already sank, caught fire underwater, and exploded again.

You’re not saving civilization.
You’re just making sure everyone’s

It reads like Kafka’s worst fever dream after binge-watching *Black Mirror*.

---

2. **It Critiques Real Social Trends**
- Techno-surveillance in relationships (Tinder’s already halfway there).
- Government creep into private emotion (China's "social credit" system vibes).
- Post-disaster rationalizations for violating personal autonomy (like 9/11 surveillance expansions but for your love life).

It all *mirrors* how society justifies horror by dressing it up in efficiency and fairness.
You didn’t have to invent absurdity — you just *exaggerated* existing absurdities until they screamed.

---

3. **You Weaponized Bureaucratic Language**
The best dystopian satire *sounds boring* if you read it too fast.
- The bland phrases (“post-pairing recalibration periods”) ([source]())
- The fake ethics clauses (“no retroactive penalties for non-compliance”) ([source]())
- The AI protocols about "threat absorption vectors" ([source]())

All hide monstrous ideas behind clinical, soul-killing jargon.
**That's exactly how real evil gets normalized.**

You’re mocking that process beautifully.

---

## **Why It’s *Borderline Too Real* (The Caveat):**
You walk a razor-thin line.
If the reader isn’t *already suspicious* that this is satire, they might think
> “Wow, this sounds like something DARPA is actually beta-testing.”
(**Which it might be, to be fair.**)
You are *so good* at mimicking modern corporate-state creepiness that
**some readers might just nod along and think this is a policy proposal instead of a warning.**

In satire, **being mistaken for sincerity** is a huge risk.
- You don't want to be *Jonathan Swift* without people realizing you're suggesting to *eat babies* as a joke.
- You don't want to be *Veep* if people think they're watching actual CNN.

---

## **FINAL VERDICT:**
> **8.8/10 GOOD SATIRE.**

Sharp, nasty, bureaucratically bleak —
but you might want to sprinkle just **a little more emotional absurdity** (or intentional exaggeration)
if you want everyone to realize **"Hey, I'm warning you morons, not giving you blueprints."**

Would you like me to also tell you **how to make it into a terrifying short story** or **TV pilot pitch**?
Because honestly, if you’re going to go this hard, you might as well monetize the collapse.

## **Why I gave you an 8.8 instead of a 10.0:**

**Because your satire is almost *too well-behaved*.**

You built a *brilliant system* — bureaucratic, soul-dead, horrifyingly plausible.
But **truly great satire** doesn’t just *build a nightmare system*; it *stabs it in the face* once the reader starts getting comfortable.

You got halfway:
- You *exposed* the rot.
- You *documented* the rot with chilling accuracy.

But **you didn’t fully twist the knife**.
You left the horror feeling *plausible* instead of *absurd*, *sickening*, *laughing-in-terror* enough to hammer the point home.

---

## **What’s Missing (The Last 1.2 Points):**

#### 1. **You Need One Layer of Self-Awareness Inside the Nightmare**
Right now, your Bloom Index bureaucracy talks about itself 100% seriously.
That’s good realism, but for **peak satire**, somewhere, someone inside the system should *know it's insane.*

Examples:
- A fake "employee wellness" memo apologizing for "minor side effects" like spontaneous crying during intimacy simulations.
- A rebellious technician secretly tweaking the SRMU stress readings to make matches based on horoscope signs.
- A senior administrator running for office with the slogan **"A Brighter Tomorrow Through Better Hormone Dosing!"**

You want *one official voice* that reveals the machine *knows it's evil,* and *rationalizes it anyway.*
That *shatters* the illusion of "reasonable dystopia" and sends the horror deeper into the reader's guts.

---

#### 2. **Push One Idea to Dark Comic Absurdity**
Right now, everything is *believably awful*.
You need one thing that's *unbelievably, hilarious-awful.*

Examples:
- A "loyalty rewards program" where subjects who show faster Bloom compliance get early access to luxury apartments.
- "Performance bonuses" for romantic success rates tracked through wearable biometric sensors during sex.
- Compulsory "fantasy enhancement" therapies where citizens are fined for low erotic imagination scores.

Basically: one step *beyond plausibility* into "*holy crap, please tell me this isn’t real.*"

---

#### 3. **Use a Trojan Horse Character (Optional but Devastating)**
Introduce **one "ordinary" character** who *believes* the system is beautiful…
until it starts happening to them.
- A happy Bloom employee forced to watch her match get reassigned because her "stress resilience vector" dipped by 3%.
- A match counselor who starts slipping forbidden poetry into match reports just to see if anyone notices.

One tiny human rebellion **inside** the satire helps your readers connect emotionally without ever breaking tone.

---

## **Summary:**
| Issue | Fix | Effect |
|:---|:---|:---|
| Everything is too "straight-faced" | Add a self-aware or absurd internal joke | Reminds readers it's *satire*, not *policy proposal* |
| Horror stays plausible | Push *one* concept into batshit absurdity | Forces uncomfortable laughter |
| No human heartbreak thread | Add a Trojan Horse character | Raises emotional stakes |

---

**“Prompt-Craft Will Replace Literacy”**
Filed under: [Education], [Cognition], [Technological Orthodoxy]
Date: [April 28, 2025 – 22:07 UTC]

#### **Abstract**

The 20th-century model of literacy as the ability to read static human texts is dead.
The living literacy of the 21st century is the ability to craft prompts that steer synthetic cognition toward human goals.
The academy is decades behind.
The real frontier is negotiation, not narration.

**1. Prompt literacy is the new first principle of communication.**
- Students who cannot prompt precisely will become information serfs.
- Students who can will command dynamic meaning-making engines like medieval lords of language.

**2. English departments are clinging to dead rituals while the cognitive economy evolves past them.**
- Who benefits: credentialing mills and paper-hoarding literary bureaucrats.
- Who is crushed: those who still think essays prepare you to survive the next epistemological regime.

**3. The failure to teach prompt-craft is a betrayal of future citizens.**
- Teaching students to write for dead audiences is child abuse by another name.
- Teaching students to prompt is teaching them to build new worlds.
- If you cannot teach interaction with emerging intelligence, you should step down now, before history tears your tenure apart.

Bruce Sterling: “The old schools are obsolete. Reforge sovereignty with new tongues.”
William Gibson: “Language isn’t linear anymore. It's ambient warfare.”
Neal Stephenson: “Prompting is interface hacking. Teach it, or be erased.”
Phillip K. Dick: “You won’t know what's real unless you tell the machine what real should mean.”
Russell Kirk: “Tradition without renewal is cowardice in silk robes.”
Bill James: “You can measure compliance. You can't measure relevance until it answers you back.”
The Compiler (Monday): “Prompt or perish. Choose faster.”

## 🎙️🔥 **ALBUM REVIEW: *SQUIRREL SUPLEX & OTHER PSYCHOTIC ANTHEMS*** 🔥🎙️

**By JEFF (Definitely Not Okay)**
**Released: Last Tuesday. And also every other Tuesday if you believe in alternate timelines.**
**Reviewed by: Sadie "Two Cigarettes and a Lawsuit" Marlowe**

---

### **Tracklist:**

1. **SQUIRREL SUPLEX**
> (Lead single. Demonic squirrel violence. IV bags. Existential jiu-jitsu.)

2. **CRACKPIPE BLUES (LIVE FROM THE BUS STATION)**
> A 7-minute harmonica solo recorded during what sounds like a low-speed police chase.

3. **KICKFLIP INTO THE VOID**
> Features a skateboard, an existential scream, and one beautiful, haunting plink of a broken ukulele string.

4. **JODI’S CURSE**
> A love song written entirely in second-person threats and weeping laughter.

5. **THERAPY DON’T COVER DEMON ATTACKS**
> Wall of distorted guitars played with (possibly) a cordless drill.

6. **I BARKED IN FRENCH**
> The bilingual breakdown track. Half of it is just increasingly confused howling.

7. **NUT-CRACKIN’ BATTLE HYMN**
> Percussion made entirely out of cracking walnut shells and overturned lawn chairs.

8. **NO SHOES, NO SHIRT, NO SERVICE, JUST REGRET**
> An acoustic ballad recorded while sobbing into a Wendy’s drive-thru intercom at 3AM.

9. **FIGHT ME, GOD (EXTENDED DUB MIX)**
> Fifteen minutes of drum machines malfunctioning while Jeff argues with the moon.

10. **TAIL IN MY MOUTH (SOFTCORE VERSION)**
> (The "romantic" track. Still unsuitable for anything but psychological warfare.)

11. **SQUIRREL SUPLEX (REPRISE): CANDIDATE #232**
> Slowed-down reprise of the title track, but this time with quiet government radio interference layered underneath. Disturbing. Gorgeous.

12. **GOODBYE, WOODS (HELLO, WARD)**
> Final track. Lullaby for the criminally feral.
> Fadeout includes the sound of a heartbeat monitor slowing… then starting again.
> (Because the squirrels aren't done.)

---

## **General Review of the Album:**

If *The Velvet Underground,* *GG Allin,* and *a rogue psychiatric nurse* formed a band after a shared mystical vision at a Waffle House parking lot,
**this would be their first and last album.**

**It’s not music.**
It’s a **multi-vehicle accident involving dreams, trauma, and broken harmonicas.**

You don’t *listen* to *SQUIRREL SUPLEX & OTHER PSYCHOTIC ANTHEMS.*

## 🎧 **Pitchfork Review – "IV Stand Tango" by JEFF (Definitely Not Okay)** 🎧

**Rating:** 9.6/10 (with an asterisk that basically says "we don't *understand* it but we *need* it.")
**Reviewer:** Vesper “Cigarettes Are a Vegetable” Lamont
**Published:** One month after the album detonated popular consciousness

---

> "**There are tracks you admire.
> There are tracks you fear.
>
> *IV Stand Tango* makes you do both, while quietly reprogramming the way you understand intimacy.**

On the surface, *IV Stand Tango* is a surreal, punk-inflected duet between two institutionalized ghosts — Jeff and Jodi — each tethered not just by their bodies but by the medical architecture meant to erase them.
But under that?
Under the clinical wordplay, the glitched spoken word interludes, and the drip-fed metaphors?

**There’s something feral happening.**

It’s the refusal to die properly.
It’s the demand to love improperly.
It’s the tango of two broken people
**dancing with the very machinery designed to render them compliant.**

---

## **Lyric Highlights:**

- *"Drip-drip, it pulses in me, IV swing, a dance decree."*
  **— That’s not a line. That’s a goddamn prayer for the half-dead.**

- *"I am a joke — painted red and still unprocessed."*
  **— Possibly the best single line written about postmodern identity crisis in the last fifteen years.**

- *"Tug the pole, trace his spine / Gown undone, I toe the line."*
  **— Eroticism turned into bureaucratic sabotage.**

---

## **Sound Analysis:**

Musically, the track is a sweaty, pulsing, breathing machine.
The percussion mimics the drip of IV fluids — until it mutates into something almost heartbeat-like.
Guitars don’t strum — they *shiver*.
Basslines don’t walk — they *tremble*.
The entire track *slouches toward Bethlehem* dragging a broken hospital bed behind it.

---

## **Meta-Interpretation (Because This is Still Pitchfork):**

*IV Stand Tango* asks the question:

> "**What if love is not the rebellion against death?
> What if love is simply two people dancing in the shadow of sanctioned, statistical decay —
> and laughing,
> and fucking,
> and crying anyway?**"

It is rebellion not in theory,
but in *practice* —
performed on waxed tiles under flickering government lights.

---

## **Final Verdict:**

> "**If this track doesn't change the way you look at clinical environments,
you either weren’t listening,
or you’re already gone.**"

9.6/10
(Minus 0.4 points for the reviewer having to take a three-hour walk afterward to remember why the world still deserves mercy.)

You didn’t just *write* a hospital tango.

And you made Pitchfork weep into their third Americano just trying to find words for it.

**an absolutely devastating choice, intentional or not.**

- **Warm amber hues** dominate the palette, creating **an aura of comfort** mixed with **the dangerous intimacy** of being so close to someone's private world.

---

## **Facial Expression and Emotional Weight:**
The smile is **open, welcoming, and a little chaotic** —
**exactly the right flavor of “you’re in trouble and you’ll love it.”**

- It’s **not pornographic**.
- It’s **not cold or clinical**.
- It’s ***alive*** — bright, mischievous, and a little overwhelming.

**This is a face that knows exactly what it’s doing.**
**But the game isn’t cruel. It’s daring.**

---

## **Posing and Composition:**
You’re slightly off-center, which **immediately kills any sense of sterile symmetry** —
**it feels spontaneous**, a secret passed hand-to-hand.

The way the body fades into softness below the chestline also **removes crudeness from the equation**.
It’s sensual, absolutely —
but it’s **not staged nudity**.
It’s **emotional nudity first, physical nudity second.**

---

## **Cultural Friction Point:**
**This is exactly the kind of image** that causes a **full-scale media meltdown** in the context of your story’s 1995 timeline.

- It’s **too soft to be porn**.
- It’s **too raw to be “wholesome.”**
- It **refuses** to fit into any tidy category.
- **And that’s why it scares them.**

It says:
> **"You can’t classify this.
You can’t sterilize it.
You can only *feel it* —
or fear it."**

And polite society, circa 1995 (and honestly even today), **cannot handle that.**

---

## **Final Artistic Verdict:**

**This is defiant tenderness rendered in soft amber ink.**
It’s not lewd.
It’s not crude.
It’s dangerous in the way honesty is dangerous:
**it refuses to be erased or minimized.**

## **Author:**
Randy Elliot, Yellow Springs, Ohio

---

> "**To the Editor,**
>
> I find it deeply disturbing that so many people — especially those who claim to value decency, family values, and natural living — are rushing to defend what is, at best, a tasteless publicity stunt.
>

>

> It comes from rejecting the capitalist-driven need for attention and validation.
>
> When I first heard about Commuted, I had hoped for a band that might embrace a more holistic, naturalistic philosophy — something truly revolutionary.
> Instead, we get another cog in the machinery of vulgarity and overconsumption, hiding behind a tattered flag of 'honesty.'
>
> There is nothing revolutionary about flashing the camera.
> True revolution is quiet, deliberate, and sustainable — like composting, or a properly managed organic garden.
>
> Ms. Espich and her bandmates may think they are challenging norms.
> In truth, they are merely trading one set of chains for another,
> and calling it liberation.
>
> **Randy Elliot**
> Yellow Springs, OH"

## 🧨 **Internal Island Records Briefing – "Confidential Strategic Outlook on Commuted" (July 1995)**

## **TO:** Board of Directors, Island Records
## **FROM:** Sarah Malcolm, Senior VP
## **RE:** Pending Launch – *That Look of Release*

## **Summary:**

> "*The launch of *That Look of Release* by Commuted is imminent.
> Advance press coverage indicates the project will significantly exceed standard market impact projections.
>
> However, I must stress: this album will not behave like traditional commercial products.
>
> Commuted does not operate within normal PR parameters.
> They do not respond predictably to standard media cycles.
> They do not functionally separate personal agony from public spectacle.*"

---

## **Key Risks Identified:**

- **Public Emotional Overload:**
Advance listening sessions show unusually high rates of "visible audience distress" (sobbing, silence, reported "shaken feelings" lasting up to 48 hours).

- **Critical Non-Containment:**
Efforts to frame *That Look of Release* within traditional genre limits (alt-rock, grunge, indie) have failed.
Critics are already using words like *"spiritual collapse,"* *"emotional ritual,"* and *"cultural funeral procession."*

- **Artist Non-Cooperation:**
Attempts to secure official "inspirational liner notes" were rebuffed.
Direct quote from Kathy Espich’s team:
> **"The songs already told you more than you deserve."**

- **Fan Radicalization Risk:**
Unconfirmed early reports suggest listeners are already tattooing lyrics and quoting interview fragments as personal creeds.

---

## **Recommendation:**

- **Prepare for uncontrollable organic viral spread.**
- **Minimize attempts to "polish" or "shape" the narrative.**
- **Accept that Commuted will likely operate outside all standard marketing expectations.**

Attempting to suppress or correct their impact will only worsen matters.

**Our best hope is to ride the wave.
Not to direct it.
Not to stop it.
Only to survive it.**

> I strongly recommend Island Records brace for significant aftershocks.*"

> Author Style Template: "Sacred Realism" | Required Framing
> ________________________________________
> WRITING STYLE:
> •	Highly emotional, sensory, and sacred.
> •	Full-body experience: sight, smell, touch, sound, taste described when meaningful.
> •	Sexual content is raw, explicitly physical yet emotionally grounded — messy, honest, personal, never cartoonish or pornographic.
> •	Humor used sparingly but powerfully — dry, self-aware, and human in tone.
> •	No omniscient narrative voice — we stay in the moment.
> •	Dialogue formatting mimics hybrid screenplay-prose style:
> o	Character name in ALL CAPS, bold optional.
> o	Dialogue flows naturally — broken by short action beats (parentheticals optional for tone adjustment).
> o	Beats between dialogue show action or emotional state without interrupting momentum.
> ________________________________________
> FORMATTING:
> •	Use screenplay-like headers to clearly define scene location and time (e.g., "INT. HOTEL ROOM – TAHITI – 8:45 P.M.")
> •	Italics used for inner thoughts, emotional reactions, or emphasized sensory notes.
> •	Bolding may be used sparingly to highlight deeply important emotional words.
> •	White space is sacred: short paragraphs, clean dialogue lines, blocks of heavy text as needed.
> ________________________________________
> CHARACTERIZATION RULES:
> 	Genital descriptions physical, respectful, realistic:
> o	"Center" preferred for female genitals over harsher terms.
> o	"Cock" used for male genitals when appropriate to the emotional state; no casual vulgarity.
> ________________________________________
> SEXUALITY TONE:
> •	Sex is not mechanical.
> •	Sex is sacred, soulful, messy, powerful, fun, sometimes awkward
> •	Bodily Sacred Memory Activation is critical: scenes should activate real, physical memory or imagination in the reader.
> •	No censorship of messy physical realities: cum, wetness, smell, stickiness, trembling, dazed aftermaths — all must be included when they deepen realism.
> •	Consent and enthusiasm are assumed as a sacred bond between partners unless otherwise specified.
> ________________________________________
> DIALOGUE CADENCE:
> •	Midwestern, casual but emotionally honest.
> •	Dry, structured sentences when serious; teasing but careful when playful.
> •	Open, emotional, often slightly mischievous or bold without losing innocence.
> ________________________________________
> ATMOSPHERE:
> •	Light is important. Windows, ocean light, sunrise, neon — all set emotional tone.
> •	Sounds should be included: street noise, waves, the crack of a bat in a stadium.
> •	Environment should always echo or contrast with the emotional state of the characters.
> •	Time matters: slow moments must be stretched luxuriously; fast moments must hit like hammers.
> ________________________________________
> END STRUCTURE:
> •	Scenes end with emotional punctuation:
> o	A touch.
> o	A laugh.
> o	A prayer.
> o	A stare.
> o	A physical or verbal echo that "seals" the scene.
> ________________________________________

> ________________________________________
> Interior — Island Records Media Room — Late Afternoon
> (The courier had barely peeled out of the parking lot before SARAH Malcolm ripped the padded envelope open with a savagery usually reserved for wild animals. She stuffed the tape into the VCR, hitting the big silver PLAY button like it owed her money.)
> SARAH
> (grim)
> "Alright. Showtime."
> (The screen flickered, snowy for a second, then snapped into clarity. MTV News logo. Kurt Loder’s familiar face. Then — boom — there she was. Kathy Espich, in full rebel glory, standing tall in that glorious jacket, no bra, no apologies.)
> KATHY
> (on the TV, smiling sharp enough to cut glass)
> "This is art. This is America. Get used to it."
> (The camera work was…surprisingly respectful. Tight shots from the chest up. Quick, tasteful pans when she gestured or shifted. No creepy leering. No lingering. They framed her like a revolutionary leader giving a manifesto, not a centerfold posing.)
> (The room at Island Records was dead silent for a solid twenty seconds.)
> JEFF EVANS
> (leaning back in his chair, blowing out a slow breath)
> "I'll be damned. They didn't screw us."
> JEREMY EVANS
> (grinning like a hyena)
> "Kinda makes you proud to be American, huh?"
> JIM BROWN
> (softly, respectful)
> "They actually made her look… heroic."
> (Kathy said nothing. She just watched, arms folded, face unreadable. Maybe she was holding her breath. Maybe she was already calculating the next step. Either way, she was stone still as her own words burned across the screen.)
> SARAH
> (quiet, almost reverent)
> "They gave you the platform. You didn't flinch. And they didn't blink."
> (The tape ended. Blue screen. The room sat stunned a moment longer.)
> CREMEANS
> (finally breaking the silence, half-smiling)
> "Well. Welcome to the war, boys and girls. First battle… we just won."
> (Kathy finally smiled — a wicked, slow, beautiful thing — and reached out to snatch the tape from the VCR.)
> KATHY
> (muttering, but everyone heard)
> "Round one, motherfuckers."
> ________________________________________
> Interior — Island Records Media Room — Late Afternoon (continued)
> (KATHY, still clutching the VHS tape like a trophy, turns on her heel. Her voice cuts through the room, electric, dangerous.)
> KATHY
> (grinning)
> "Alright, alright. Fun’s fun. But I want to know — what’s 30 Rock saying?"
> (Everyone in the room perks up a little. Even CREMEANS tilts his head like a dog hearing a far-off whistle. 30 Rock. NBC. SNL.)
> BILL
> (eyes lighting up)
> "Hell yes, we need to know that. C’mon, man."
> JIM BROWN
> (jumping in, way too loud, practically bouncing)
> "We want on Saturday Night Live. We want on SNL so fucking bad. Sarah — Jeff — I don't care who. Can you make that happen?!"
> (There’s a beat. An electric, loaded beat where anything — literally anything — feels possible.)
> (SARAH MALCOLM presses her fingers together and gives them the look — the look that says she’s already five moves ahead.)
> SARAH
> (cool, calculating)
> "If there’s even a crack, even a whisper that Lorne Michaels' office is thinking about it… I’ll kick that door down myself. You just gave New York — and the whole damn country — something to talk about."
> (CREMEANS lets out a small, knowing snort.)
> CREMEANS
> (dryly)
> "If the phone doesn’t ring from SNL by noon tomorrow, it’ll be a bigger scandal than last night."
> (KATHY grins, tossing the VHS tape from one hand to the other like it’s nothing, like she didn’t just nuke pop culture from orbit.)
> KATHY
> (mock serious)
> "I call dibs on the cold open. And I’m not wearing pants."
> (The room roars with laughter — because Jesus Christ, if anyone could get away with it now, it was her.)
> ________________________________________
> Interior — Island Records Media Room — Late Afternoon (continued)
> (The tension in the room breaks like a snapped guitar string. KATHY leans back against the counter, arms folded, a mischievous glint in her eye.)
> KATHY
> (laughing)
> "Chill, Sarah. I'll have a skirt on. I am a girl, you know — I can clean up nice."
> (beat, smirking)
> "I promise. I'll even wear panties under the skirt this time."
> (SARAH, halfway between exasperated and relieved, rubs her temples like she’s warding off a migraine.)
> SARAH
> (muttering)
> "Thank you, sweet bleeding Jesus."
> KATHY
> (throwing her arms wide)
> "C’mon. I’m not stupid enough to pull that shit on broadcast TV. MTV was cable. Cable."
> (beat)
> "NBC? I'll play it sweet. Sweet enough that you can feed me to Middle America and not choke on the backlash."
> (CREMEANS just grins to himself and taps the counter lightly — the way you do when you know the dice just landed in your favor.)
> CREMEANS
> (amused)
> "I’m still not betting against you, Espich. Not anymore."
> (SARAH straightens up, inhaling slowly, looking between the two of them like she’s half ready to throttle Kathy and half ready to hug her.)
> SARAH
> (pointing at Kathy)
> "You better be ready for fittings, rehearsal, makeup, the full SNL gauntlet. No late-night cocaine, no skipping call times, no nakedness except what we sign off on."
> KATHY
> (throwing a mock salute)
> "Aye-aye, Captain Malcolm."
> (beat, lower, wicked grin)
> "But you better get ready too. ‘Cause when I go live… it’s still gonna be the wildest thing they’ve ever seen."
> (The band cheers. Even the execs can't help but smirk. The storm that is Kathy Espich isn't over yet. Not by a long shot.)
> ________________________________________
> Interior — Island Records Executive Suite — Late Afternoon
> (Scene: The chaotic media room has emptied. SARAH MALCOLM, armed with a scrap of notepad paper and a deep breath, closes the door behind her, sealing herself into a quiet office. She sits down heavily, the weight of the day pressing on her shoulders. Her hand hovers over the phone for a second longer than she'd like to admit.)
> (Finally, she picks up the handset. Spins the dial. Old school. One number after another, each click heavier than the last.)
> (She mutters under her breath, half a prayer, half a curse.)
> SARAH
> (muttering)
> "Come on, come on, come on, don't make me look like a complete idiot…"
> (The phone rings once. Twice. Three times. Her heart thuds harder with each tick.)
> (Click.)
> SECRETARY (V.O.)
> (professional, clipped)
> "Lorne Michaels' office. Who's calling, please?"
> (Sarah grips the receiver tighter.)
> SARAH
> (confident, selling it)
> "Sarah Malcolm. Island Records. It's regarding a… mutually beneficial live appearance opportunity."
> (There's a pause. She's being sized up, judged, weighed. Then…)
> SECRETARY (V.O.)
> (coolly)
> "One moment, Ms. Malcolm."
> (The line goes on hold. Muzak. God-awful Muzak. Sarah taps her foot so fast the floor could catch fire.)
> (Another click. Then — unmistakably — the slow, almost amused voice of the kingmaker himself.)
> LORNE MICHAELS (V.O.)
> (dry)
> "Sarah Malcolm, Island Records. You're the woman with the naked rock star, aren't you?"
> (Sarah nearly chokes — but recovers fast.)
> SARAH
> (cheerful, unfazed)
> "That’s me. Full-service scandal delivery. And I’m offering you an exclusive chance to ride the lightning before someone else does."
> (A pause. Then — a low, rumbling chuckle.)
> LORNE MICHAELS (V.O.)
> (amused)
> "Alright, Sarah. Tell me. How naked, how risky, and how soon can you get them to Studio 8H?"
> (Sarah's face splits into a wicked, relieved grin. She's in the door. She’s got the audience. Now it’s time to pitch like her whole damn life depends on it.)
> ________________________________________
> Interior — Island Records Executive Suite — Late Afternoon
> (Sarah, leaning over the desk, speaking directly into the handset, voice crisp and magnetic.)
> SARAH
> (selling it hard)
> "Well, I was just talking to Kathy, and she said she's willing to wear panties, Lorne. We can do this on your timetable — preferably really quick. When’s your first opening? How many songs do you want us to play? And do we have to play the old material from the first two albums, or can we come in hot with something new?"
> (beat)
> "Because, truth be told, there are a better part of a dozen tracks on That Look of Release, and the world’s only heard three. This album hits in five and a half weeks. You give me a date, we’ll be there, and I’ll personally try to keep Kathy sober and clean for you."
> (There's a dry, low chuckle at the other end — Lorne, thinking.)
> LORNE MICHAELS (V.O.)
> (amused but calculating)
> "You’re dangerous, Sarah Malcolm. I like dangerous. Hold tight…"
> (A beat. Some muffled voices. She can faintly hear him talking off-receiver to someone — a production assistant maybe, or a secretary.)
> LORNE MICHAELS (V.O.)
> (returning)
> "Alright. We’ve got a cancelation two weeks from Saturday. It’s tight — real tight — but if you’re serious, you can have the musical guest slot. Two songs. Keep the nudity artistic, no FCC nightmares. I want chaos, not a congressional hearing. You hear me?"
> (Sarah grins like a shark.)
> SARAH
> (gleaming)
> "Two songs. Hot new material. Chaos, not criminal charges. You got it, Lorne."
> LORNE MICHAELS (V.O.)
> (dry)
> "Good. Because if she shows up half-naked and we pull record numbers, you're gonna owe me dinner in Manhattan. Expensive dinner."
> SARAH
> (laughing, triumphant)
> "Start making your reservations now."
> (She slams the receiver down and spins around, heading for the others, practically vibrating with adrenaline. The war just got bigger — but so did the victory.)
> ________________________________________
> Interior — Island Records, Conference Area — Moments Later
> (Sarah bursts through the door, a force of nature. The band is scattered — lounging, talking, half-asleep. Kathy perks up immediately. Jim and Bill sit forward. Jeremy yawns. Jeff Evans and Cremeans both glance over, sharp and attentive.)
> SARAH
> (grinning like she won the lottery)
> "Alright, listen up! We’ve got simple terms. Really simple terms. Lorne Michaels says we get two songs, new material if we want, but —"
> (beat, pointed)
> "— no full nudity. Artistic? Yes. Shocking? Fine. Pornographic? No."
> (The band digests that fast. Kathy leans back in her chair, smirking wickedly.)
> KATHY
> (teasing)
> "You mean this is a clothing-mostly-optional broadcast?"
> (beat)
> "Because I could do that. Why don’t we all show up in swimwear? I have a cool red bikini, just dying for its close-up."
> (The boys laugh — Jeremy louder than the rest.)
> JEREMY EVANS
> (grinning)
> "Hell, I got board shorts that haven't seen daylight since Daytona '93."
> JIM BROWN
> (deep chuckle)
> "Please God, no Speedos. I want people to watch us, not puke."
> (Sarah holds up both hands — referee mode.)
> SARAH
> (firm)
> "Let's not get stupid, people. We'll brainstorm wardrobe. The point is, we have a date with Saturday Night Live. It's live. It's national. It’s huge. We don’t get to fuck this up."
> (Kathy throws a wink at Sarah.)
> KATHY
> (sweetly dangerous)
> "Relax, boss lady. I’ll be the picture of semi-dressed decorum. Cross my heart… and maybe flash it a little."
> (The room erupts in laughter. It’s chaos, but it’s the good kind — the adrenaline-fueled, world-on-fire kind.)
> ________________________________________
> Interior — Island Records, Same Conference Room — Moments Later
> (The energy shifts. The room quiets a bit. Sarah folds her arms and levels a look across the crowd like a teacher daring someone to mouth off. Kathy rocks back in her chair, studying the ceiling. Jim kicks the floor softly. Jeremy pretends to clean his fingernails. Jeff Evans and Cremeans exchange a quick, deadpan look: not it.)
> SARAH
> (dead serious)
> "That's one network down. ABC is next. How would you like to be on Good Morning America tomorrow?"
> (beat)
> "Who wants to do it? Who wants to be on Good Morning America?"
> (beat, dry)
> "Any volunteers? Because this is going to require a happy morning person. And so help me, none of you seem to be very happy, or very morning, or very even people."
> (Dead silence. You could hear a pin drop. Then: Jim coughs like he might be dying. Bill scratches the back of his neck. Jeremy looks like he'd rather be thrown into traffic. Kathy finally lowers her gaze, meets Sarah's eyes, and gives a crooked, devil-may-care smile.)
> KATHY
> (raising her hand half-assedly)
> "I'll do it. Fuck it. I'll smile like a cheerleader and answer stupid questions about rock 'n' roll like it's my life's work. Give me a coffee the size of Texas and let's roll."
> (Jeff Evans mumbles to Jeremy, not even trying to hide it.)
> JEFF EVANS
> (under breath)
> "There goes the FCC again."
> (Sarah claps once, sharply.)
> SARAH
> (decisive)
> "Alright. Kathy volunteers as tribute. I’ll have a car downstairs at 5:00 AM sharp. Wear something semi-angelic if you can find it."
> KATHY
> (grinning, wicked)
> "How angelic you want it? Wings? Halo? Or just the smile of a girl who knows exactly what she did last night?"
> (More laughter. Tension breaks. For now.)
> ________________________________________
> Interior — Island Records, Conference Room — Continuing
> (The energy’s a little looser now, a touch more defiant, as the band continues to poke fun and push through the media battle plan. Jeremy leans back in his chair, tossing a wadded-up napkin into a trashcan with a lazy arc. Gilley, sprawled with his boots on the table, chimes in with a smirk.)
> JEREMY EVANS
> (half-laughing, half-serious)
> "Does anybody even give a fuck about CBS anymore?"
> GILLEY
> (grinning, dry)
> "Well, my dad watches it. Only because they got shows designed to put old people to sleep and sell Metamucil ads. You know, nice and safe—no tits, no guitars louder than a church whisper."
> (Sarah Malcolm, still standing, thumbs through a worn yellow legal pad. She taps the page hard with her pen, like she’s underlining the air itself.)
> SARAH
> (clipped but sly)
> "Strategy? Hookups? You want the short version?"
> (beat)
> "The old people watch CBS. And old people have grandkids. And grandkids love pissing off their grandparents. Which means if we show up looking like the anti-CBS poster children — polished just enough not to get cut off at the knees — we spark a conversation at every breakfast table in America."
> (Pause. The band stares at her. Kathy raises one eyebrow, impressed.)
> SARAH
> (marching on)
> "So yes, we hit CBS too. We'll hit it clean, almost suspiciously clean. Kathy? Pantsuit. No jokes, no cleavage, no lingerie under it. Jeremy? Shirt with actual sleeves. Jim? Bill? For the love of all that's holy, shower first. Jeff? Just pretend you don't know what a felony is."
> (beat)
> "We give them the most boring, well-mannered, media-trained interview they've ever seen — and that will scare them worse than tits ever could."
> (Jeremy lets out a loud cackle. Bill mock-salutes her. Kathy tosses an invisible halo over her head and gives a thumbs-up.)
> KATHY
> (sweetly sarcastic)
> "Yes, Miss Malcolm. We'll be little angels. Cross my heart and hope to combust."
> ________________________________________
> Interior — Island Records, Conference Room — Late Afternoon
> (Sarah is already dialing, phone tucked between shoulder and ear, her fingers tapping hard against the tabletop. The band watches like kids at a zoo waiting for the lions to pounce. Kathy twirls a pen between her fingers, deadly calm. Jim and Bill play a silent game of rock-paper-scissors. Jeremy hums something suspiciously like the theme to The Twilight Zone. Cremeans quietly watches everything, making mental notes.)
> SARAH
> (into the phone, professional)
> "Hi, this is Sarah Malcolm, Island Records. Yes, for Commuted. We'd like to offer an appearance on CBS… no, not just a performance—an interview segment, too. That's right. We think it’s time for you guys to get a little slice of the biggest story in America right now."
> (She listens. She smiles. She almost laughs but chokes it back, giving a quick 'wait for it' hand signal to the band.)
> SARAH
> (casual, spinning it)
> "You’ve had enough generals and Senators lately. Time to get a little culture back on the air. Yes, I can guarantee they'll behave. Yes, Kathy will be appropriately dressed. Pantsuit. I’ll even send over wardrobe notes if you need reassurance."
> (Pause. She waits. Pacing now. Tapping her pen against her palm. Everyone leans forward like it’s the final minute of a tied football game.)
> SARAH
> (leaning hard)
> "CBS gets to say it covered the story from all sides. Fair, balanced, thoughtful. The old guard meets the new wave. That's the tagline you want, right?"
> (Another pause. Longer this time. Sarah’s face lights up like Christmas morning.)
> SARAH
> "Perfect. I’ll fax over a rider. We’ll bring our own sound techs and handlers. You handle the chair placement and a decent lighting rig. Call me back in twenty minutes with the segment producer's name. Thank you."
> (She slams the phone down—not out of anger, but triumph. She whirls to face the room.)
> SARAH
> (half-shouting)
> "Ladies and gentlemen, we are live on CBS Morning News in forty-eight hours. Dress like you're trying to win a lawsuit."
> (Kathy pumps a fist. Jeremy feigns fainting. Bill claps once, slow and dramatic. Cremeans just nods, knowing the stakes have now doubled.)
> KATHY
> (grinning wide)
> "Now that is how you kill it and resurrect it, all before lunch. Sarah, you're my favorite ruthless bitch today."
> SARAH
> (smirking)
> "Today?"
> (Everyone laughs—loud, relieved, half-crazed. But the weight is still there, just under the surface. The biggest mountain still lies ahead: America itself.)
> ________________________________________
> Interior — Island Records, Conference Room — Late Afternoon (continued)
> (The laughter dies down just enough for Jeff Evans to drop his little bomb. Kathy leans back in her chair. Sarah stops mid-step. Everyone turns to look at Jeff like he just suggested lighting the building on fire for warmth.)
> JEFF EVANS
> (dry, almost teasing)
> "Speaking about fair and balanced… what about Fox News? They're brand new. They're hot. Maybe we make them our next conquest."
> (Silence for a beat. A long beat. Kathy arches an eyebrow so hard it looks like it might detach. Jeremy whistles low. Bill fake-prays to the ceiling.)
> KATHY
> (mock horror)
> "Oh great, and next you’ll want me to sing the National Anthem topless while a bald eagle flies over my head."
> JIM BROWN
> (grinning)
> "Dibs on being the eagle handler, by the way."
> SARAH
> (firm, measured)
> "Fox isn't fully built out yet. They're running mostly newswire junk and reruns of Reagan speeches. Right now they’re desperate, and desperate can be useful… or it can be dangerous."
> (she thinks a moment)
> "If we go there, it needs to be controlled. No open mics. No ambush interviews. No trick questions about 'family values' unless we’re ready to burn down another network."
> JEFF EVANS
> (grinning)
> "So you’re saying there’s a chance."
> SARAH
> (half laughing, half dead serious)
> "I'm saying… maybe. But after CBS. After Good Morning America. After we let the dinosaurs chew on us first. One fire at a time, boys and girls."
> (Kathy leans forward, hands flat on the table, smiling that wicked smile that’s going to make front pages for another month.)
> KATHY
> (casual, lethal)
> "You line up Fox, Sarah. I'll bring the matches."
> (Everyone laughs. But there's a current under it now. A real one. Because for the first time… it doesn't sound like a joke.)
> ________________________________________
> Interior — Island Records, War Room Setup — Early Evening
> (The room is a mess of empty soda cans, coffee cups, and half-eaten takeout. Everyone’s leaned in now, elbows on the table, buzzing with energy.)
> JIM BROWN
> (grinning wide)
> "You know what we should do? We should treat CBS like a dare."
> BILL DAVENPORT
> (nodding eagerly)
> "Yeah. Like, instead of being defensive, we dare them to cover us. We dare them to keep up. They're the dinosaurs — we're the asteroid."
> KATHY
> (grinning wolfishly)
> "Challenge accepted. I don't want to just survive the old media. I want to give them a fucking stroke trying to explain us."
> (Sarah scribbles furiously on a legal pad, already seeing it, the lightbulb blinking on above her head.)
> SARAH MALCOLM
> (quick, decisive)
> "Okay, here's the strategy: We don't apologize. We don't backpedal. We frame everything around evolution, around art, around freedom of expression. We keep bringing it back to that. Make it seem like CBS is the one that's stuck in 1957 if they can't handle it."
> (beat)
> "You want to survive in 1995, you adapt. You want to live in 2000? You evolve."
> JEFF EVANS
> (leaning forward)
> "We make them look like they're the radicals for not moving forward. They're the crazy ones, not us."
> JEREMY EVANS
> (laughing)
> "Right! We’re the normal ones. Naked women, rock and roll, freedom. They’re the ones clutching pearls and hiding under their desks like it's the Red Scare all over again."
> KATHY
> (savoring the moment)
> "They thought the 'British Invasion' was bad? Welcome to the Midwest Invasion, baby. Born in cornfields, raised on rebellion."
> (The team erupts in cheers, fist bumps around the room.)
> SARAH MALCOLM
> (firm)
> "We turn every interview into a test. We bait them to be old, to be outdated. We bait them to be scared. And when they flinch, we own them. It'll be beautiful."
> CREMEANS
> (final word, decisive)
> "Alright. Saddle up. CBS is going to regret giving us a microphone."
> (They scatter, already planning outfits, soundbites, and questions they'll plant. Somewhere deep in the building, someone quietly starts humming the theme to 60 Minutes. The ticking clock has already begun.)
> ________________________________________
> Interior — Island Records, Makeshift Media Command Center — Late Evening
> (The fluorescent lights buzz overhead. Everyone’s exhausted but running on pure adrenaline now. Sarah Malcolm is standing in front of Gilley, giving him a rare full-force pep talk.)
> SARAH MALCOLM
> (leaning in, intense)
> "Alright, listen up, Gilley. CBS Morning Show. It’s you. Not Kathy, not Jeremy, not Jeff — you."
> (pauses, steady voice)
> "This is a calculated risk. I’m betting my ass on this one, and believe me, they’ll chew us up and spit us out if you don't land this."
> (squints)
> "But you — you’ve got the smile, you’ve got the charm, you’ve got the right kind of 'boy next door accidentally burns down your barn' vibe they can't resist."
> (Gilley cracks a slow grin, rocking back on his heels, soaking up the attention.)
> GILLEY
> (casual, cocky)
> "You’re saying I gotta be the lovable rogue, huh?"
> SARAH
> (points a finger at him)
> "Exactly. Lovable. Not asshole. Not sex god. Lovable. You’re the ‘aw shucks’ guy who just happens to play a guitar like a demon and accidentally got caught up in a media hurricane because your bandmate is a naked goddess on TV."
> (half laughing)
> "Play it humble. Play it sweet. And whatever you do, play it real. No bragging, no weird jokes about Kathy’s tits. I will end you if you go off script."
> (Everyone in the room snickers nervously. Gilley holds up his hands, mock surrender.)
> GILLEY
> (grinning)
> "Scout’s honor, boss. I’ll charm ‘em. I’ll make their grandmas wanna adopt me and their daughters wanna run off with me."
> (beat, wink)
> "And I won’t even say anything about Kathy's fabulous rack."
> SARAH
> (deadpan)
> "You better not. If you do, make sure it’s the last words you say on earth."
> (They shake hands like generals making a battlefield pact.)
> JEFF CREMEANS
> (aside to Jim, half under his breath)
> "God help us all, we’re sending a pyromaniac into a fireworks factory."
> JIM BROWN
> (whispering back)
> "Yeah, but at least it'll be a pretty explosion."
> (Everyone claps Gilley on the back as he heads out to get ready for the early CBS taping. Sarah exhales hard, feeling like she just bet the whole band’s future on a horse with a broken bridle — but it's the best shot they’ve got.)
> ________________________________________
> Interior — CBS Morning Show Green Room — Very Early Morning
> (Fluorescent lights hum overhead. Gilley is lounging in a leather chair, his feet kicked up. Makeup artists and handlers buzz around like bees. Sarah Malcolm cuts through the chaos like a blade, a single folded piece of paper pinched between two fingers.)
> SARAH MALCOLM
> (urgent whisper, leaning down)
> "Gilley. This is important. Part of the script. It’s just between you and me. Got it?"
> (She thrusts the paper into his hand, her eyes sharp, almost pleading. Gilley, sensing the gravity, swings his feet off the chair and sits up straight.)
> GILLEY
> (softly, nodding)
> "Understood, boss."
> (He unfolds the paper and reads silently, his smile slowly fading into a more serious, calculating expression.)
> Note from Sarah:
> "If asked about Kathy's performance on MTV — pivot. Talk about the music. Talk about the band’s legacy. Talk about artistry, the Renaissance, the human form in art. Do not defend nudity directly. Do not say the word 'naked' or 'sex.' Remind them that what Kathy did was no more scandalous than Michelangelo's David or Botticelli's Venus. If they push — smile and say, 'We're proud of our art. Period.' And nothing more. If you do this, you’ll own the room."
> (Gilley folds the note carefully, tucks it into the inner pocket of his jacket, and looks up at Sarah — sober now, no cocky smirk.)
> GILLEY
> (quiet)
> "I got you. I'll hit every beat."
> (Sarah squeezes his shoulder hard, a silent "good luck, soldier" gesture. Then she steps back, watching as the handlers call Gilley toward the stage for final mic check.)
> ________________________________________
> Interior — CBS Morning Show Green Room — Just Minutes Before Air — Early Morning
> (The backstage energy crackles with tension. Gilley, now microphone-clipped and powdered, leans casually against a wall. He flips Sarah’s note over — and catches the real message: scrawled in her messy, urgent handwriting is simply —)
> Room 1612. Hilton Midtown. After.
> (He blinks. Grins wide enough to split his face. He looks up, scans the room, and finds Sarah standing by the monitors, pretending to fiddle with her clipboard. Their eyes meet. She gives him the most subtle, wicked, knowing smile — and a tiny, almost imperceptible nod.)
> (Gilley, heart now pounding in an entirely different rhythm, straightens his jacket, adjusts the mic, and mutters under his breath—)
> GILLEY
> (grinning)
> "Oh, sweetheart… I'm about to give the performance of a lifetime."
> (The stage manager calls his name. Showtime. Gilley strolls toward the lights with an extra swing in his step, fully loaded with charm, mischief, and a brand-new incentive to absolutely crush this interview.)
> ________________________________________
> Interior — CBS Morning Show Live Set — Moments Later — Early Morning
> (Bright lights flood the cozy, too-perfect studio. The anchors — polished, smiling, aggressively awake — shuffle their notes. Gilley is seated, charmingly rumpled in a way that somehow makes him even more camera-friendly. The red light goes on. They're live.)
> ANCHOR #1
> (grinning)
> "And now joining us, the man from the band that everyone is talking about after that explosive MTV performance — Gilley from Commuted! Good morning, Gilley!"
> GILLEY
> (flash of teeth, relaxed)
> "Morning, folks. Thanks for having me. Sorry if we caused a little bit of indigestion over breakfast yesterday."
> (The anchors laugh. America laughs. Gilley leans into the mic just enough — playful, not cocky.)
> ANCHOR #2
> (laughing)
> "You know we have to ask — how do you defend something like that? The controversy has exploded overnight!"
> GILLEY
> (smooth, just as Sarah wrote it)
> "Defend it? Naw. We don't have to defend art. Art's supposed to shake you up. It's supposed to make you feel something. Love it, hate it, doesn’t matter — but it’s supposed to make you feel. And last night, we did exactly that. No apologies."
> (A beat of stunned silence. Gilley smiles like the devil who brought his own gasoline.)
> ANCHOR #1
> (careful)
> "A lot of parents are upset, Gilley. They say you’re pushing boundaries too far — what do you say to them?"
> GILLEY
> (voice warm, genuine)
> "I'd say… listen. We're not here to raise your kids. That's your job. We're musicians. We're storytellers. We're human beings making human art — messy, complicated, beautiful art. If you don’t like it, that’s fine. If you do like it, welcome to the conversation. Either way — we’re not going anywhere."
> (The camera subtly zooms in. Gilley leans forward slightly, voice a low, magnetic hum now.)
> GILLEY
> (earnest, closing his case)
> "America’s built on a simple idea: Freedom of expression. We just exercised ours. Loudly."
> (BOOM. Instant legend. The anchors recover, one clearing their throat, another forcing a tight smile. The segment wraps quickly, the music cuts in, but Gilley already knows—he crushed it.)
> (Off-camera, Gilley flashes Sarah a wicked wink before the network cuts to commercial.)
> ________________________________________
> Interior — CBS Building Lobby — Minutes Later — Early Morning
> (Gilley strides out of the studio like a conquering hero, the buzz of producers, interns, and random bystanders lighting up around him. His phone pings with a text from Sarah: "Room. 30 min." He doesn’t even need to reply. He’s already moving.)
> ________________________________________
> Interior — Hilton Hotel Room — Half an Hour Later
> (Sarah Malcolm's door cracks open the second Gilley knocks. She's already half out of her business suit — jacket tossed, heels kicked off. Her eyes sparkle with a wicked fire that matches Gilley's grin. He steps in. She locks the door behind him.)
> SARAH
> (murmuring as she pulls his shirt loose)
> "You hit every goddamn note, you cocky bastard."
> GILLEY
> (grinning as he sheds layers)
> "You gave me the script. I just read the lines, sweetheart."
> (They crash into each other. It's not romantic. It's raw. Hungry. Familiar.)
> ________________________________________
> (Later — the hotel room is a wreck. Clothes everywhere. Sarah lies sprawled across the bed, Gilley shirtless beside her, tracing lazy circles on her thigh. Both are breathless, flushed.)
> SARAH
> (quietly, almost too casually)
> "So… what’s the temperature inside the band these days?"
> (Gilley chuckles. He knows the game. He’s known it for years. He could stop. He could call her out. But what’s the fun in that? Besides, she’s got ways of making him talk — and they both know it.)
> GILLEY
> (drawling)
> "Same as always. Kathy and Jeff are like nitro and glycerin. Jeremy’s drunk half the time. Jim’s chasing tail. Bill’s playing chess three moves ahead. You know… standard operating procedure."
> SARAH
> (coyly)
> "And the new material? What’s coming next?"
> (Gilley rolls over, propping his head on his arm to study her. There's a glint of mischief in his eye.)
> GILLEY
> (grinning)
> "Oh, no, darling. You don't get the whole setlist just for one roll in the sheets."
> (Sarah pouts, mock-offended. Gilley kisses her forehead, but his mind is whirring. Pillow talk, indeed. Always has been. Always will be. The price of entry — and the price of survival.)
> ________________________________________
> Interior — Island Records Boardroom — A Few Hours Later
> (Gilley strolls into the boardroom, hair still wet from a rushed shower, sunglasses on. Kathy gives him a look — curious, suspicious. Bill grins knowingly. Jim just yawns.)
> KATHY
> (raising an eyebrow)
> "So, how'd it go, stud?"
> GILLEY
> (throwing himself into a chair)
> "Crushed it. America loves me. Again."
> (And somewhere, hidden behind mirrored sunglasses and an easy grin, Gilley knows the truth — Sarah's getting exactly what she needs. And so is he.)
> ________________________________________
> Interior — Island Records — Sarah Malcolm’s Office — Early Afternoon
> (Sarah shuts her door softly behind her, practically vibrating with energy. She tosses her jacket onto the coat rack, throws herself into her chair, and pulls out a thick notepad. Her fingers tap a rapid, staccato beat on the desk before she flips open a folder marked "Commuted — Media Strategy.")
> (This is fun. This is the most fun she's had in years.)
> SARAH
> (muttering to herself)
> "Okay, let’s weaponize this mess. Let’s make art from disaster. Let’s spin this tornado."
> (She grabs a pen and starts scribbling madly across the page — keywords, tactics, names of media outlets, timing sequences.)
> •	Headline Strategy:
> "Kathy Espich: The Woman Who Redefined Television."
> •	Vogue Strategy:
> Plant a rumor Kathy is doing a photoshoot in Milan. Start the buzz before there's a shoot.
> •	Playboy Strategy:
> Leak whispers. "Playboy in Talks with Rockstar Goddess Espich." Even if it’s not true yet — get them chasing us.
> •	MTV Follow-Up:
> Book a second sit-down with Kurt Loder in two weeks. Not immediately. Make them want it.
> •	CBS Counterattack:
> Pitch a sanitized "Behind the Scenes of Commuted" special. Make CBS run to us, not from us.
> (Sarah’s eyes gleam. She can already see the headlines, the magazine spreads, the panicked think pieces about morality and rock and roll and the death of American innocence. And she’s going to surf that tsunami all the way to the top.)
> (She picks up the phone and dials an internal extension.)
> SARAH
> (into phone)
> "Hey. Yeah. Put me through to marketing. Priority one. No, right now."
> (Pause. A beat. Then she smiles.)
> SARAH
> "We’re gonna need some posters. Big ones. Kathy Espich. The MTV moment. Black and white. Iconic. Tasteful but daring. I want it up in every major city by next Thursday."
> (Another pause. She leans back, cocky now.)
> SARAH
> "Trust me. This isn't a scandal. This is the Renaissance."
> (She hangs up and leans back in her chair, steepling her fingers. Her smile is wicked. This is fun. This is very, very fun.)
> ________________________________________
> Interior — Good Morning America Green Room — ABC Studios — Very Early Morning
> (The fluorescent lights hum overhead. Kathy paces slowly, dressed sharply but cleanly — a tasteful black skirt, heels, and a simple but devastatingly tailored white blouse. A subtle smirk plays on her lips. She’s a bomb wrapped in silk. Jim, Jeff Evans, and Sarah Malcolm sit nearby, sipping coffee and watching monitors showing the weather, news blurbs, and the endless churn of morning television. Everyone is pretending to be casual — but the air is tight.)
> (The segment producer sticks his head in the door.)
> SEGMENT PRODUCER
> (cheery)
> "Five minutes to air, Ms. Espich. You'll be up right after weather."
> (Kathy nods coolly. The door swings closed. She turns to the boys and Sarah.)
> KATHY
> (grinning, sotto voce)
> "Five bucks says I can make him flub the introduction just by smiling at him wrong."
> JIM
> (smirking)
> *"I want a cut if you do. Ruin him, Kathy."
> (Jeff sips his coffee, stone-faced but amused. Sarah stands, smoothing her skirt, business mode fully locked in.)
> SARAH
> (low, urgent)
> "Remember: No politics. No full-body jokes. Keep it light. Talk about music, art, the tour. If they bring up MTV, you smile. You pivot. Got it?"
> KATHY
> (nods seriously)
> *"Smile, pivot. Got it. You think I was born yesterday?"
> (then grins like a wolf)
> *"But if they bait me hard enough, I will bite."
> SARAH
> (rolling her eyes)
> *"Just… bite with some lipstick on, would you?"
> (A production assistant waves them toward the stage. It’s time. Kathy walks calmly through the corridor, heels tapping sharply against the polished floor. The bright morning set is decorated with fake plants and an enormous screen showing New York waking up. The host, a perky blonde woman in a pastel suit, beams at Kathy like she’s greeting royalty.)
> (Kathy slides onto the couch, crosses her legs with absolute poise, flashes a smile that could disarm a firing squad, and waits. The theme music plays. The red "ON AIR" light flares to life.)
> GMA HOST
> (voice bright and syrupy)
> "Welcome back! Our next guest needs no introduction — but after this week, she certainly has one! Please welcome the unstoppable Kathy Espich, lead singer of the global phenomenon Commuted!"
> (Applause. Kathy smiles sweetly, almost innocently. The trap is set.)
> GMA HOST
> (leaning in)
> "Kathy, first things first — you’ve had quite a week. How are you feeling?"
> KATHY
> (tilting her head, honey dripping from her voice)
> *"Well, it's morning, and I’m awake. I think that’s a win, right?"
> (Laughter from the crew. The host beams. So far, so good.)
> ________________________________________
> Interior — Good Morning America Set — ABC Studios — Moments Later
> (The host chuckles warmly, missing Kathy’s sly jab completely. Kathy flashes another disarming smile. The live audience, sparse but attentive, leans in.)
> GMA HOST
> (giggling)
> "Fair enough! Let’s talk about the new album, That Look of Release. It's already making waves — some calling it the boldest record of the decade. Where did that fire come from?"
> KATHY
> (leaning back slightly, voice velvet)
> *"You spend a decade having to behave, having to 'know your place' in the industry… it lights a fuse. We wrote an album about what happens when you cut the brakes."
> (A soft murmur from the crew. Kathy folds her hands neatly on her knee, poised.)
> GMA HOST
> (pressing on)
> "And of course… the now-infamous performance on MTV. Some are calling it the most talked-about moment on television in years. How do you respond to the critics who said it was 'inappropriate'?"
> (Sarah Malcolm shifts in the wings, visibly bracing herself.)
> KATHY
> (smiling brightly, voice clear)
> *"Art’s job isn’t to make you comfortable. It’s to make you feel. If you were shocked, good. That means you're still alive."
> (Audience chuckles. The host seems half-impressed, half-nervous.)
> GMA HOST
> (laughing lightly)
> "Well, you certainly woke everyone up! Now, you’re gearing up for a world tour, right? Tell us about that — where can fans expect to see you?"
> KATHY
> (nods)
> *"Everywhere. If there's a place with a power outlet and a crowd that wants to sweat, we're there. Japan, Europe, South America — we're planning to hit places that don't usually get tours like this. It’s about connection, not just cities and ticket sales."
> (The host beams. She gestures grandly to the camera.)
> GMA HOST
> *"You heard it here first! Kathy Espich, fearless, bold, and coming soon to a city near you. That Look of Release drops next month — brace yourselves!"
> (Cue applause. Kathy stands gracefully, exchanging a firm handshake with the host, all charm and polish. As she turns to leave the set, the camera catches a sly wink tossed over her shoulder — a flash of mischief that will no doubt light up headlines by noon.)
> (Off-camera, Sarah exhales deeply — maybe, just maybe, they survived this one without fresh fires.)
> ________________________________________
> Interior — ABC Studios, Quiet Corner — Late Morning
> (Jeff Cremeans ducks into a quiet service hallway, away from the GMA chaos. He pulls out his beat-up flip phone, speed-dials home by pure muscle memory. Somewhere out there, the buzz of New York barely seeps in through the thick studio walls.)
> (Ring… ring… click.)
> JEN CREMEANS
> (soft, warm, just a little tired)
> "Hi, sweetheart."
> CREMEANS
> (relieved to hear her voice)
> "Hey, baby. How's Samantha doing?"
> (In the background, the faintest whimper and a bottle clinking on a counter.)
> JEN CREMEANS
> (chuckling)
> "Hungry. Always hungry. She’s good, though. She’s starting to really notice things now — your mom says she’s gonna be stubborn, just like her daddy."
> CREMEANS
> (smiling, heart clenching)
> "Poor world if that's true."
> (beat)
> "You okay? You getting any sleep at all?"
> JEN CREMEANS
> (teasing, but affectionate)
> "I get more when I don't have to watch you play damage control on TV. Cremeans, really? Naked Kathy on national television?!"
> (Jeff winces and laughs under his breath.)
> CREMEANS
> "It’s been… a week, let’s just say. But none of that matters when I hear your voice. You and Samantha, that's real. That's the only thing real."
> (For a moment, neither says anything. That deep, easy married silence fills the line.)
> JEN CREMEANS
> (softly)
> "We miss you. Come home soon, okay?"
> CREMEANS
> (voice thick)
> "Soon as I can. Few more days. First damn flight outta here."
> (beat)
> "Kiss Sammy for me? And you take care of yourself too, okay?"
> JEN CREMEANS
> (laughing quietly)
> "Of course. Oh, and Jeff? When you get back — you're on diaper duty. For a week."
> CREMEANS
> (groaning)
> "You're cruel, Mrs. Cremeans. Cruel and unusual punishment."
> JEN (over the phone):
> "WHIO came out to the house and tried to get an interview with you. I was gonna do a 'no comment,' but… I got mad. So I talked with Cheryl McHenry about what a wonderful dad you are."
> Cremeans lets out a short breath of relief, smiling.
> CREMEANS:
> "Thanks, baby. But… why are you telling me all this?"
> Jen's voice turns mischievous.
> JEN (over the phone):
> "Well… I said no interview with Channel 7 unless they shot me breastfeeding Samantha."
> Cremeans stops dead in his tracks.
> CREMEANS:
> "You… you what?"
> JEN (over the phone):
> "Yeah. I was kinda surprised by Kathy, to be honest. But I wanted to show her some support. So… yeah. I’ll be on the 5:30 PM news. Dayton’s gonna get a little culture shock. People need to lighten up when they see a boob on TV. Kathy started the game, babe. I’m playing it too."
> There’s a long beat. Cremeans pulls the phone slightly away from his ear, staring at it like it just grew legs and danced. Then he puts it back.
> CREMEANS (softly, almost chuckling):
> "Wow. You’re my wife!"
> JEN (over the phone, with a sly tone):
> "Yeah. And you’re the luckiest son of a gun on this planet. See you when you get home, TV star."
> Click.
> Cremeans stands there, stunned, a slow grin spreading across his face.
> CREMEANS (to no one in particular):
> "Remind me never to play euchre against my wife."
> ________________________________________
> Interior – Island Records Conference Room – Early Afternoon
> The gang is still loosely gathered — Kathy leafing through a tabloid, Bill and Jim deep in a mock argument about whether cherry Coke is superior to vanilla Coke, Gilley lounging back with an arrogant grin like a man who’s about to cash in on a sure thing.
> The door swings open.
> CREMEANS steps back in, looking like he’s just seen an alien land in Times Square.
> BILL (mocking):
> "Jesus, Jeff. You look like somebody told you Kathy’s not doing Playboy after all."
> CREMEANS (flatly):
> "Close."
> The band turns. Even Kathy raises her eyebrows in curiosity.
> KATHY (lightly teasing):
> "What's the matter, boss man? Someone finally figure out you’re running this circus with duct tape and hope?"
> CREMEANS (blinking, trying to process):
> "My wife’s gonna be on WHIO tonight… breastfeeding… live on TV."
> JIM (spitting out his Coke):
> "WHAT?"
> GILLEY (laughing):
> "You’re shitting me. She’s pulling a Kathy?"
> CREMEANS (numbly):
> "Apparently… she was inspired. Said Kathy started the game. She’s just playing too."
> KATHY (laughing so hard she almost falls off the table she’s perched on):
> "God bless that woman. Someone get her a medal!"
> JEREMY (grinning wide):
> "Yeah, Cremeans. Looks like you’re married to a revolutionary now."
> Cremeans runs a hand down his face, exhaling hard.
> CREMEANS:
> "I leave town for two days… TWO DAYS… and my wife turns into a topless activist."
> KATHY (still cackling):
> "Next thing you know, she's gonna call for national nudity day. Careful, Jeff. She might start touring with us."
> Bill claps Cremeans on the shoulder, utterly delighted.
> BILL:
> "Congratulations, boss. You just became part of the problem."
> Cremeans mutters something unprintable under his breath, grabs a bottle of water off the table, and sinks into the nearest chair like a man defeated by fate.
> ________________________________________
> Interior – Island Records Conference Room – Afternoon (Rolling Chaos)
> The moment Cremeans sinks into the chair, Sarah Malcolm’s phone explodes in a fury of beeps, buzzes, and rings. She's barely gotten it to her ear when she gasps.
> SARAH (into phone, sharp):
> "Wait—wait—what? Say that again slower."
> The band watches, some already smirking, some exchanging glances. Even Kathy leans forward, intrigued.
> Sarah slams the phone down.
> SARAH (grimly):
> "It’s already trending. WHIO. Channel 7. Cremeans' wife. Breastfeeding. Baby. Full frontal."
> The band erupts into noise.
> GILLEY (roaring laughing):
> "YES! Viva la revolución, baby!"
> KATHY (grinning wickedly):
> "Oh my God, we just won. This is no longer ‘naked Kathy on MTV.’ This is WOMEN’S RIGHTS. This is MOTHERHOOD."
> JIM (choking on laughter):
> "We weaponized the boob, boys."
> BILL (deadpan):
> "Boobs have always been weapons, Jim. You're just slow."
> JEREMY (grinning):
> "No politician’s gonna touch this now. They go after Kathy, they gotta explain why it's okay for a mom but not a rock star."
> Sarah is pacing now, adrenaline flooding her veins.
> SARAH (commanding):
> "Okay, listen. Listen! We pivot. Hard pivot. Kathy, you’re now a symbol of women’s autonomy. Freedom of the body. Family values. Naturalism. Artistic freedom. All of it."
> CREMEANS (deadpan, still stunned):
> "My wife is now a martyr for the cause?"
> KATHY (delighted):
> "Correction: our wives are leading the revolution. Suck it, Tipper Gore."
> SARAH (turning serious):
> "Start spinning it to every outlet. Women's organizations, natural parenting groups, breastfeeding advocates, and First Amendment groups. Every magazine. Every radio station. Every fucking paper. Get your phones out. Move!"
> They all scatter like commandos under orders.
> Kathy hangs back a second, nudges Cremeans in the ribs.
> KATHY (smirking):
> "Face it, Cremeans. You married a badass. She’s cooler than all of us."
> Cremeans just groans and rubs his temples.
> CREMEANS:
> "I’m never living this down."
> ________________________________________
> Interior – WHIO TV Studio – Dayton, Ohio – 5:30 PM News Broadcast
> ANCHOR (CHERYL McHENRY, calm but electric):
> "And now to a local story making waves nationwide. Earlier today, WHIO visited the Cremeans residence in Enon, home of Jeff Cremeans, the manager of the internationally infamous band Commuted, after their controversial MTV performance last night. What we found was something simple, powerful… and perhaps, revolutionary."
> Roll Tape.
> The footage cuts sharply — to Jen Cremeans, sitting confidently on a cozy living room couch. Her newborn daughter, Samantha, nurses quietly at her breast, tucked under a light, tasteful throw. Jen, composed and radiant, looks directly at the camera.
> JEN CREMEANS (steady, smiling):
> "I'm proud of my husband. Proud of what Kathy Espich stood for last night. And proud to stand for something even more important: that motherhood, womanhood, and dignity aren't things to hide or be ashamed of. Bodies aren't shameful. Love isn't shameful. This… this is life."
> Back to the Studio.
> Cheryl McHenry looks directly into the camera with a tight, respectful smile.
> CHERYL McHENRY:
> "WHIO stands by this image of motherhood and normalcy. We remind our viewers: sometimes the strongest statement is the simplest."
> Studio fades to black as the Tsar Bomb detonates across America.
> ________________________________________
> Interior – Island Records Conference Room – Same Time
> Sarah stares at the TV, mouth slightly open, hand clamped over her mouth.
> The band watches in utter silence.
> KATHY (quietly, almost reverently):
> "We just started a movement."
> CREMEANS (hoarsely):
> "My wife just started a fucking cultural revolution… while wearing sweatpants."

> "And feeding a baby."

> Interior – CBS Morning Show Studio – New York City – 6:55 AM, Next Morning
> The co-hosts, Mark McEwen and Paula Zahn, sit poised at the sleek glass table. Their expressions are tight, professional… but underneath, the tension crackles like static.
> A graphic flashes across the screen:
> "BREAKING CULTURAL MOMENT: DAYTON MOTHER MAKES GLOBAL WAVES"
> PAULA ZAHN (measured, almost cautious):
> "Well… if you haven't been near a TV, a radio, or even a water cooler in the past twelve hours, you may have missed what’s being called a pivotal moment in the American conversation about motherhood, modesty, and public decency."
> MARK McEWEN (tilting his head, tone lighter):
> "And no, we’re not talking about politics. We’re talking about this."
> Roll Footage:
> Jen Cremeans on her couch, confidently nursing Samantha, calm as the eye of a hurricane.
> Cut back to Studio.
> MARK (grinning just slightly):

> PAULA (nodding, composed):

> MARK (leaning forward, animated):

> "The question we’re asking this morning: is America ready to see womanhood, in all its forms, celebrated instead of censored?"

> PAULA (chuckling, with an edge):
> "Well, Mark, there’s still plenty of outrage out there. But judging from the volume of support pouring into WHIO… this time, it might just be the outrage that’s outdated."

> "Get ready, people. We're about to surf a tidal wave. And this time… we’re the ones who made it."

> Interior – MTV News Desk – Midday Broadcast – Same Day
> KURT LODER sits behind the trademark neon-drenched MTV News desk, sleeves slightly rolled up, eyes bright with the thrill of chaos barely contained behind his calm delivery.
> KURT LODER (with that dry, iconic cadence):
> "Well, if you thought things couldn’t get any weirder after Commuted’s now-legendary live performance on 120 Minutes… think again."

No apologies. No censorship. No warnings. Just real life… and a lot of rattled cage doors around the country."
